## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of population (dP_dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population density and possibly time-varying environmental factors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Malthusian exponential growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited resources, constant per-capita growth rate'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreases logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population has a minimum viable size (strong Allee effect)'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Generalized density-dependent growth with fractional scaling'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth'}
- {'name': 'Time-modulated logistic', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with time-varying carrying capacity or growth rate'}
- {'name': 'Exponential decay of growth rate in time', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Per-capita growth rate changes exponentially over time (environmental degradation/improvement)'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Saturating reproduction minus density-dependent mortality'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Polynomial expansion of density-dependent effects including higher-order interactions'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → multiplicative factor (1 - P/K) or similar rational/polynomial correction to linear growth
- Allee effects (positive density dependence at low P) → cubic or higher-order polynomial in P with sign changes, e.g., P*(P-c1)*(c2-P)
- Cooperative or fractional metabolic scaling → non-integer power laws P**c with c ≠ 1
- Time-varying environment → multiplicative or additive functions of t modulating the growth rate, e.g., sin(c*t) or exp(c*t) prefactors
- Logarithmic saturation → log(c/P) factor indicating Gompertz-type asymptotic approach to carrying capacity
- Competition for resources → negative P**2 terms representing pairwise interactions reducing growth
- Ratio of production to loss → difference of two power-law terms c0*P**a - c1*P**b representing anabolism vs catabolism
- Saturating reproduction → Michaelis-Menten-like term P/(P+c) in the growth rate indicating resource limitation per individual

Expanding:
```
= 0.5980*P - 0.5980*P²/32.94 + 0.5980*P - 0.5980*P*exp(-0.0768*P)
= 1.196*P - 0.01816*P² - 0.5980*P*exp(-0.0768*P)
```

So GT = **a*P² + b*P + c*P*exp(d*P)** where a < 0, b > 0, c < 0, d < 0.

The key basis functions are: **P², P, P·exp(negative·P)**. There's no dependence on `t`.

Let me now check each candidate for structural compatibility.

For a candidate to match, it must be expressible as `α·P² + β·P + γ·P·exp(δ·P)` with appropriate constants.

**Candidates with `t` dependence that can't be zeroed out:** Many candidates include `t` terms. If `t` appears only as `c*t` additive terms, we can set those coefficients to 0. But if `t` is embedded in a way that can't be eliminated, it's NO MATCH.

**Candidates with log, sin, or other non-exp basis functions:** These cannot match since log(P...) and sin(...) are linearly independent from exp(P).

Let me systematically go through:

**Candidates with P*exp(P*c) terms (potential matches):**

**Candidate 1:** `P*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*sin(c5*log(P*c6+1)+c7)`
Has exp(P*c3) but not P*exp(P*c3). Also has sin(log(...)). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 10:** `P*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*log(c5*exp(P*c6)+1)`
log(c5*exp(P*c6)+1) is a softplus-like function, not equivalent to P*exp(P). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 17:** `P*c0 + P*c1*((P*c2)^c3 - 1) + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6)`
= P*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2)^c3 - P*c1 + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6). Has P*(P*c2)^c3 = c1*c2^c3 * P^(c3+1) and exp(P*c6) but not P*exp(P*c6). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 18:** `P*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6)`
= (c0+c1)*P + c3*P^c2 + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6). No P*exp term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 19:** `P*c0 + P^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(P*c5)`
Similar - has exp(P*c5) but not P*exp(P*c5). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 25:** `P*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*log(P*c5+1)`
No P*exp term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 28:** `P*c0 + c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*exp(P*c5)`
Two exp terms but no P*exp. However, can two exponentials approximate P*exp? No - we need exact match. But wait: c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*exp(P*c5). GT needs P² + P + P*exp(dP). These are different basis functions. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 41:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(P^c4*c5)`
If c4=1, this becomes P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(P*c5). Still exp(P*c5), not P*exp(P*c5). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 47:** `P*c0*(P*c1+1)*(c2*t+1) + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5*t + c6`
Set c2=0, c5=0: P*c0*(P*c1+1) + c3*exp(P*c4) + c6 = c0*c1*P² + c0*P + c3*exp(P*c4) + c6. Has exp not P*exp. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 48:** `P*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2+1)*(c3*t+1) + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6)`
Set c3=0: P*c0 + P*c1*(P*c2+1) + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6) = c1*c2*P² + (c0+c1)*P + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6). Same issue. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 50:** `P*(P*c0+c1) + P^c2*c3 + c4*exp(P*c5)`
= c0*P² + c1*P + c3*P^c2 + c4*exp(P*c5). If c2=1: (c0)P² + (c1+c3)P + c4*exp(P*c5). Still exp not P*exp. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 57:** `P*c0 + P*c1*(P+c2) + c3 + c4*exp(P*c5)`
= c1*P² + (c0+c1*c2)*P + c3 + c4*exp(P*c5). Same issue. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 58:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4`
Same - exp not P*exp. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 61:** `P*(P*c0 + c1 + c2*log(P*c3+1)) + c4*exp(P*c5)`
= c0*P² + c1*P + c2*P*log(P*c3+1) + c4*exp(P*c5). Has P*log and exp, not P*exp. NO MATCH.

Now let me look at **rational function candidates** that might simplify:

**Candidate 77:** `(P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + c3)/(P + c4)`
This is a rational function. Performing polynomial division:
P³*c0/(P+c4) = c0*P² - c0*c4*P + c0*c4²  - c0*c4³/(P+c4)
So result = c0*P² + (c1-c0*c4)*P + (c2+c0*c4²-c1*c4) + (c3-c0*c4³+c1*c4²-c2*c4)/(P+c4)

This gives P² + P + constant + 1/(P+c4). The term 1/(P+c4) cannot equal P*exp(dP). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 78:** Similar rational. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 88:** `P*(P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2)/(P + c3)`
= P*(c0*P² + c1*P + c2)/(P+c3). Polynomial division gives P*(c0*P + (c1-c0*c3) + (c2-c3*(c1-c0*c3))/(P+c3))
= c0*P² + (c1-c0*c3)*P + (c2-c3*c1+c0*c3²)*P/(P+c3). This has P/(P+c3) term, not P*exp. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 89:** Similar. NO MATCH.

Now let me look at candidates with **P^c** terms (power law):

**Candidate 49:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*exp(P*c5) + 1`
Has P^c2 and exp(P*c5). Neither is P*exp(P). NO MATCH.

Let me reconsider. The GT has the form P² + P + P*exp(αP). Can any candidate produce P*exp(αP)?

Looking at candidates with explicit `exp(P*c)` multiplied by P:

**Candidate 4:** `P*(P*c0 + P*c1*exp(P*c2) + c3 + c4*log(P*c5+1))`
= c0*P² + c1*P²*exp(P*c2) + c3*P + c4*P*log(P*c5+1)
Has P²*exp not P*exp, and P*log. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 26:** `(c0 + (P*c1+c2)*(P*c3+c4+c5*exp(P*c6)))/(P*c1+c2)`
= (c0 + (P*c1+c2)*(P*c3+c4+c5*exp(P*c6)))/(P*c1+c2)
= (P*c3+c4+c5*exp(P*c6)) + c0/(P*c1+c2)
= P*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(P*c6) + c0/(P*c1+c2)
Has exp(P*c6) and 1/(P*c1+c2), not P*exp. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 27:** `(P*c0 + c1 + (P*c2+c3)*(P*c4+c5+c6*exp(P*c7)))/(P*c2+c3)`
= (P*c0+c1)/(P*c2+c3) + P*c4 + c5 + c6*exp(P*c7)
Has exp(P*c7) and rational term. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 40:** `(P*c0 + (P+c1)*(P*c2+c3+c4*exp(P*c5)))/(P+c1)`
= P*c0/(P+c1) + P*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(P*c5)
Has exp(P*c5) and P/(P+c1). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 37:** `P*c0*(P*c1+1)*(c2*t+1) + c3*t + c4 + c5*exp(P^c6*c7)`
Set c2=0, c3=0, c6=1: c0*c1*P² + c0*P + c4 + c5*exp(P*c7). Still exp not P*exp. NO MATCH.

Let me look more carefully. Is there ANY candidate that has P*exp(P*c)?

Looking through all candidates again... None seem to have an explicit P*exp(P*c) term.

Wait - let me reconsider candidates with `P^c2*c3` where c2 could be non-integer. But P^c2 is a power law, not P*exp(αP). These are fundamentally different functions. NO MATCH for all such candidates.

Let me check **Candidate 87:** `P*(P*c0+c1) + c2*exp(c3/P^(1/3))`
exp(c3/P^(1/3)) ≠ P*exp(αP). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 56:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c3*log(c4*exp(P*c5)+1)`
log(c4*exp(P*c5)+1). For large P*c5, this ≈ P*c5 + log(c4). For small, ≈ log(c4+1). This is a softplus, not equivalent to P*exp(αP). NO MATCH.

**Candidate 53:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*log(c5*exp(P*c6)+1) + 1`
Same softplus issue. NO MATCH.

**Candidate 54:** `P*(P*c0+c1) + P^c2*c3 + c4*log(c5*exp(P*c6)+1)`
Same. NO MATCH.

After exhaustive analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the basis function P*exp(αP) that is required by the GT. The candidates contain exp(P*c), log(...), sin(...), P^c, rational functions, etc., but none have the specific P*exp(αP) term.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking all remaining candidates I haven't explicitly analyzed... Going through the full list confirms no candidate has P*exp(αP) as a term.
